### Subsection: 11.1b Role of Economic Development in Brownfield Redevelopment

Economic development plays a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment. It involves the strategic planning and implementation of policies and programs to promote economic growth and improve the quality of life in a community. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, economic development can help to identify potential sites for redevelopment, secure funding for remediation and redevelopment, and attract new businesses and investments.

One of the key roles of economic development in brownfield redevelopment is identifying potential sites for redevelopment. Economic development agencies often work closely with local governments and community organizations to identify abandoned or underutilized properties that have the potential for redevelopment. This can involve conducting site assessments and feasibility studies to determine the viability of redevelopment and the potential economic impacts.

Economic development also plays a crucial role in securing funding for brownfield redevelopment. The process of remediating and redeveloping brownfield sites can be costly, and often requires a combination of public and private funding. Economic development agencies can help to secure grants and loans from government agencies and private organizations to cover the costs of remediation and redevelopment. They can also work with developers and investors to attract private funding for brownfield projects.

Finally, economic development can help to attract new businesses and investments to redeveloped brownfield sites. By promoting the economic benefits and opportunities of brownfield redevelopment, economic development agencies can attract businesses and investors who are interested in locating in the revitalized areas. This can lead to job creation, increased tax revenue, and overall economic growth in the surrounding communities.

In conclusion, economic development plays a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment by identifying potential sites, securing funding, and attracting new businesses and investments. By working together with other stakeholders, economic development agencies can help to maximize the economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment and contribute to overall economic development in the surrounding areas. 


### Section: 11.1 Economic Impacts of Brownfields:

Brownfield redevelopment has the potential to bring about significant economic impacts in the surrounding areas. By revitalizing abandoned or underutilized properties, brownfield redevelopment can stimulate economic growth, create jobs, and attract new businesses and investments. In this section, we will explore the various economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment and how they contribute to overall economic development.

#### 11.1a Overview of Economic Impacts

The economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment can be seen at both the local and regional levels. At the local level, brownfield redevelopment can bring about direct economic benefits, such as job creation and increased property values. This is especially important for communities that have been struggling with blighted and contaminated properties, as brownfield redevelopment can help to revitalize these areas and attract new residents and businesses.

At the regional level, brownfield redevelopment can have a ripple effect on the economy. By creating jobs and attracting new businesses, brownfield redevelopment can contribute to overall economic growth and development in the surrounding areas. It can also help to diversify the local economy and reduce dependence on a single industry or sector.

One of the key economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment is job creation. The process of brownfield redevelopment involves a range of activities, such as site assessment, remediation, and redevelopment planning, which require a diverse set of skills and expertise. This creates job opportunities for a variety of professionals, including environmental engineers, urban planners, and construction workers. Additionally, the new businesses and industries that are attracted to the redeveloped brownfield sites can also create jobs in the surrounding areas.

Another economic impact of brownfield redevelopment is increased property values. By revitalizing blighted and contaminated properties, brownfield redevelopment can improve the overall aesthetic and desirability of the surrounding area. This can lead to an increase in property values, benefiting both homeowners and the local government through increased property tax revenue. In addition, the presence of new businesses and industries can also contribute to an increase in property values, as they bring in more economic activity and potential for growth.

#### 11.1b Economic Development through Brownfield Redevelopment

In addition to the direct economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment, there are also indirect economic benefits that contribute to overall economic development. These include increased tax revenue, improved public health and safety, and enhanced community pride and identity.

One of the main ways in which brownfield redevelopment contributes to economic development is through increased tax revenue. As mentioned earlier, the revitalization of blighted and contaminated properties can lead to an increase in property values, resulting in higher property tax revenue for the local government. In addition, the new businesses and industries that are attracted to the redeveloped brownfield sites can also generate tax revenue through sales and income taxes.

Another indirect economic benefit of brownfield redevelopment is improved public health and safety. By remediating contaminated sites, brownfield redevelopment can reduce the risk of exposure to hazardous substances and improve the overall health and well-being of the community. This can lead to a decrease in healthcare costs and an increase in productivity, both of which contribute to economic development.

Lastly, brownfield redevelopment can also enhance community pride and identity. By revitalizing abandoned or underutilized properties, brownfield redevelopment can improve the overall appearance and livability of the community. This can instill a sense of pride and ownership among residents, leading to a stronger sense of community and potentially attracting new residents and businesses.

#### 11.1c Case Studies in Economic Development and Brownfield Redevelopment

To further illustrate the economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment, let's take a look at some real-world case studies.

One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel plant in Bethlehem, Pennsylvania. The site, which was once the second-largest steel producer in the country, had been abandoned for over a decade and was heavily contaminated with hazardous substances. Through a partnership between the local government and private developers, the site was remediated and redeveloped into a mixed-use development, including residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This project not only created thousands of jobs but also brought in millions of dollars in tax revenue for the local government.

Another successful brownfield redevelopment project is the transformation of the former Stapleton International Airport in Denver, Colorado. The site, which had been abandoned for over a decade, was redeveloped into a sustainable community with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This project not only created thousands of jobs but also contributed to the economic growth of the surrounding area, attracting new businesses and investments.

These case studies demonstrate the potential for brownfield redevelopment to bring about significant economic impacts and contribute to overall economic development. By revitalizing abandoned or underutilized properties, brownfield redevelopment can create jobs, increase property values, and generate tax revenue, while also improving public health and safety and enhancing community pride and identity. 


### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment not only has the potential to bring about significant economic impacts, but it can also be a powerful tool for economic development. In this section, we will explore the various economic development strategies that can be used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment to maximize its potential.

#### 11.2a Overview of Economic Development Strategies

Economic development strategies are plans and actions taken by governments, organizations, and communities to stimulate economic growth and improve the standard of living in a particular area. These strategies can range from targeted investments in specific industries to policies that promote entrepreneurship and innovation.

One of the most common economic development strategies used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment is tax incentives. These incentives can include tax breaks, tax credits, and tax abatements for businesses that choose to locate or expand in a redeveloped brownfield site. These incentives can help to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment, making it more attractive for businesses to invest in these areas.

Another strategy is the creation of economic development zones. These are designated areas that offer a range of benefits and incentives to businesses, such as streamlined permitting processes, access to funding and resources, and infrastructure improvements. By designating a brownfield site as an economic development zone, it can become more attractive for businesses to invest in and can help to spur economic growth in the surrounding area.

In addition to these strategies, partnerships between public and private entities can also be a powerful tool for economic development. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to attract new businesses and investments to redeveloped brownfield sites. This can also help to create a more sustainable and diverse economy in the long term.

Overall, the combination of brownfield redevelopment and economic development strategies can have a significant impact on the local and regional economy. By revitalizing blighted and contaminated properties, creating jobs, and attracting new businesses and investments, brownfield redevelopment can be a catalyst for economic growth and development. It is important for communities to carefully consider and implement these strategies to maximize the potential of brownfield redevelopment and create a more prosperous future.


### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment not only has the potential to bring about significant economic impacts, but it can also be a powerful tool for economic development. In this section, we will explore the various economic development strategies that can be used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment to maximize its potential.

#### 11.2a Overview of Economic Development Strategies

Economic development strategies are plans and actions taken by governments, organizations, and communities to stimulate economic growth and improve the standard of living in a particular area. These strategies can range from targeted investments in specific industries to policies that promote entrepreneurship and innovation.

One of the most common economic development strategies used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment is tax incentives. These incentives can include tax breaks, tax credits, and tax abatements for businesses that choose to locate or expand in a redeveloped brownfield site. These incentives can help to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment, making it more attractive for businesses to invest in these areas.

Another strategy is the creation of economic development zones. These are designated areas that offer a range of benefits and incentives to businesses, such as streamlined permitting processes, access to funding and resources, and infrastructure improvements. By designating a brownfield site as an economic development zone, it can become more attractive for businesses to invest in and can help to spur economic growth in the surrounding area.

In addition to these strategies, partnerships between public and private entities can also be a powerful tool for economic development. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to attract new businesses and investments to redeveloped brownfield sites. This can also help to create a more sustainable and diverse economy in the local community.

#### 11.2b Selection of Economic Development Strategies

When it comes to selecting the most appropriate economic development strategies for a brownfield redevelopment project, there are several factors that should be considered. These include the goals and objectives of the project, the characteristics of the site, and the needs and priorities of the local community.

One important consideration is the type of industry or businesses that the community is looking to attract. For example, if the goal is to revitalize a struggling manufacturing sector, then targeted investments and tax incentives may be the most effective strategies. On the other hand, if the goal is to promote innovation and entrepreneurship, then policies that support small businesses and startups may be more appropriate.

The characteristics of the brownfield site itself can also play a role in the selection of economic development strategies. For instance, if the site has significant environmental contamination, then tax incentives and grants may be necessary to offset the high costs of remediation. Alternatively, if the site is located in a prime location with access to transportation and a skilled workforce, then creating an economic development zone may be the most effective strategy.

Finally, it is important to consider the needs and priorities of the local community when selecting economic development strategies. This can include factors such as job creation, affordable housing, and community revitalization. By involving community stakeholders in the decision-making process, the selected strategies can better align with the needs and goals of the community.

In conclusion, the selection of economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment projects should be carefully considered and tailored to the specific goals, characteristics, and needs of the project and the local community. By utilizing a combination of strategies and involving all stakeholders in the decision-making process, brownfield redevelopment can not only bring about economic benefits but also contribute to the overall well-being and sustainability of the community.


### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment not only has the potential to bring about significant economic impacts, but it can also be a powerful tool for economic development. In this section, we will explore the various economic development strategies that can be used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment to maximize its potential.

#### 11.2a Overview of Economic Development Strategies

Economic development strategies are plans and actions taken by governments, organizations, and communities to stimulate economic growth and improve the standard of living in a particular area. These strategies can range from targeted investments in specific industries to policies that promote entrepreneurship and innovation.

One of the most common economic development strategies used in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment is tax incentives. These incentives can include tax breaks, tax credits, and tax abatements for businesses that choose to locate or expand in a redeveloped brownfield site. These incentives can help to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment, making it more attractive for businesses to invest in these areas.

Another strategy is the creation of economic development zones. These are designated areas that offer a range of benefits and incentives to businesses, such as streamlined permitting processes, access to funding and resources, and infrastructure improvements. By designating a brownfield site as an economic development zone, it can become more attractive for businesses to invest in and can help to spur economic growth in the surrounding area.

In addition to these strategies, partnerships between public and private entities can also be a powerful tool for economic development. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to attract new businesses and investments to redeveloped brownfield sites. This can also help to create a more sustainable and diverse economy in the local community.

#### 11.2b Tax Incentives for Brownfield Redevelopment

As mentioned earlier, tax incentives are a commonly used economic development strategy in conjunction with brownfield redevelopment. These incentives can take various forms, such as tax breaks, tax credits, and tax abatements. The goal of these incentives is to make it more financially feasible for businesses to invest in redeveloping brownfield sites.

Tax breaks refer to a reduction in the amount of taxes that a business must pay. This can include exemptions from certain taxes, such as property taxes or sales taxes. Tax credits, on the other hand, are a direct reduction in the amount of taxes owed. For example, a business may receive a tax credit for a percentage of the costs incurred during the remediation and redevelopment of a brownfield site. Tax abatements are a temporary suspension or reduction of taxes, often used as an incentive for businesses to invest in a particular area.

These tax incentives can be crucial in making brownfield redevelopment financially viable for businesses. The costs of remediation and redevelopment can be significant, and these incentives can help to offset those costs and make the project more attractive to potential investors.

#### 11.2c Case Studies in Economic Development Strategies

To further illustrate the effectiveness of economic development strategies in brownfield redevelopment, let's take a look at some case studies.

One successful example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Bethlehem, Pennsylvania. This site was once a thriving steel mill but had been abandoned for over a decade, leaving behind contaminated land and dilapidated buildings. Through a partnership between the city, state, and private developers, the site was transformed into a mixed-use development with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This project not only created jobs and brought in new businesses, but it also revitalized the surrounding community.

Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Packard Automotive Plant in Detroit, Michigan. This site had been abandoned for decades and was a symbol of the city's decline. Through a combination of tax incentives, grants, and partnerships, the site was transformed into a mixed-use development with residential, commercial, and industrial spaces. This project not only brought new economic opportunities to the area but also helped to revitalize the surrounding neighborhoods.

These case studies demonstrate the potential of economic development strategies in brownfield redevelopment. By utilizing a combination of tax incentives, partnerships, and creative planning, these sites were able to be transformed into thriving economic hubs, bringing new opportunities and growth to their respective communities.

#### 11.2d Conclusion

In conclusion, economic development strategies are crucial in maximizing the potential of brownfield redevelopment. By offering tax incentives, creating economic development zones, and fostering partnerships, these strategies can make it more financially feasible for businesses to invest in redeveloping brownfield sites. The success of these strategies is evident in the numerous case studies of successful brownfield redevelopment projects. As we continue to address the issue of brownfields, it is essential to consider the economic benefits and opportunities that can be achieved through effective economic development strategies.


### Section: 11.3 Economic Development and Community Engagement:

Community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will explore the importance of community engagement and how it can be integrated into economic development plans.

#### 11.3a Role of Community Engagement in Economic Development

Community engagement refers to the process of involving and empowering community members in decision-making processes that affect their lives. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, community engagement is essential for several reasons.

Firstly, community engagement allows for the identification of community needs and priorities. By involving community members in the decision-making process, economic development strategies can be tailored to address the specific needs and priorities of the community. This not only ensures that the strategies are effective but also increases community support and buy-in.

Secondly, community engagement can help to build trust and foster positive relationships between stakeholders. Brownfield redevelopment often involves multiple stakeholders, including government agencies, private developers, and community members. By involving community members in the decision-making process, it can help to build trust and promote collaboration between these stakeholders.

Thirdly, community engagement can lead to more sustainable and equitable economic development. By involving community members, economic development strategies can be designed to benefit the entire community, rather than just a select few. This can help to create a more inclusive and equitable economy, where all members of the community can benefit from the redevelopment of brownfield sites.

There are several ways in which community engagement can be integrated into economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment. One approach is to involve community members in the planning and decision-making process from the beginning. This can include conducting community surveys, hosting public meetings, and forming community advisory committees. By involving community members from the start, it ensures that their voices are heard and their needs are considered in the development of economic strategies.

Another approach is to incorporate community benefits agreements (CBAs) into economic development plans. CBAs are legally binding agreements between developers and community organizations that outline the benefits and commitments that the developer will provide to the community in exchange for their support. These benefits can include job training programs, affordable housing, and environmental remediation efforts. By including CBAs in economic development plans, it ensures that the community directly benefits from the redevelopment of brownfield sites.

In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial component of economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the decision-making process, it can lead to more effective, sustainable, and equitable economic development.

This can include hosting community meetings and workshops to gather input and feedback from community members. By involving them in the planning process, community members can have a say in the type of development that takes place in their neighborhood, ensuring that it aligns with their needs and priorities.

Another technique for engaging the community in economic development is through the use of community benefits agreements (CBAs). CBAs are legally binding agreements between developers and community organizations that outline the benefits that the community will receive in exchange for supporting the development project. These benefits can include job training programs, affordable housing, and environmental remediation efforts. In addition to these techniques, it is also important to ensure that the community is kept informed and updated throughout the entire economic development process. This can be done through regular communication and transparency from the developers and government agencies involved in the project. By keeping the community informed, it can help to build trust and promote a sense of ownership and involvement in the project.

Overall, community engagement is a crucial aspect of economic development for brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the decision-making process and ensuring that their needs and priorities are addressed, it can lead to more successful and sustainable redevelopment projects that benefit the entire community.

We have seen how the revitalization of contaminated sites can bring about economic benefits to a community, such as job creation, increased property values, and tax revenue. We have also discussed the challenges and considerations that must be taken into account when redeveloping brownfields, including the potential for environmental hazards and the need for community involvement and support.

Overall, it is clear that brownfield redevelopment can be a valuable tool for promoting economic growth and revitalizing communities. However, it is important to approach these projects with caution and careful planning to ensure that they are carried out in a sustainable and responsible manner. By incorporating environmental management practices into the redevelopment process, we can not only achieve economic success, but also protect the health and well-being of both current and future generations.

## Chapter: Brownfield Redevelopment and Social Equity

### Introduction:

In recent years, there has been a growing concern for the environmental and social impacts of urban development. Brownfield sites, which are abandoned or underutilized properties with potential environmental contamination, have become a major focus for environmental management and redevelopment efforts. While the remediation and redevelopment of brownfield sites can bring economic benefits to a community, it is important to consider the potential social equity implications of these projects.

This chapter will explore the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and social equity. We will discuss the definition of social equity and its importance in environmental management. We will also examine the potential social impacts of brownfield redevelopment, including displacement of low-income and minority communities, and the role of community engagement in addressing these issues.

Furthermore, this chapter will delve into the various strategies and tools that can be used to promote social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. These may include affordable housing requirements, job training programs, and community benefits agreements. We will also discuss the challenges and limitations of implementing these strategies, as well as potential solutions.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the relationship between brownfield redevelopment and social equity. By considering the social impacts of these projects and implementing strategies to promote equity, we can ensure that brownfield redevelopment is not only environmentally sustainable, but also socially responsible. 


### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss the various ways in which brownfield redevelopment can affect social equity.

#### 12.1a Overview of Social Impacts

Before delving into the specific social impacts of brownfield redevelopment, it is important to define the concept of social equity. Social equity refers to the fair distribution of resources, opportunities, and privileges among all members of a society. This includes access to education, healthcare, housing, and employment, among other things. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, social equity means ensuring that all members of a community, regardless of their socioeconomic status or race, have equal access to the benefits and opportunities that come with these projects.

One of the main social impacts of brownfield redevelopment is the potential displacement of low-income and minority communities. As brownfield sites are often located in economically disadvantaged areas, the redevelopment of these sites can lead to gentrification and rising property values, making it difficult for long-time residents to afford to stay in their homes. This can result in the displacement of these communities, leading to a loss of social ties and community cohesion.

Furthermore, brownfield redevelopment can also have a negative impact on the health and well-being of residents in the surrounding area. The remediation process can release harmful pollutants into the air and water, potentially causing health issues for nearby residents. In addition, the construction and operation of new developments can also contribute to noise and air pollution, further impacting the quality of life for residents.

In order to address these social impacts, it is crucial to involve the community in the brownfield redevelopment process. Community engagement can help to ensure that the needs and concerns of residents are taken into consideration and that the benefits of the project are shared equitably. This can include involving community members in decision-making processes, providing opportunities for job training and employment, and incorporating affordable housing into the redevelopment plans.

In addition to community engagement, there are various strategies and tools that can be used to promote social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. These may include affordable housing requirements, which can help to ensure that new developments include affordable units for low-income residents. Job training programs can also be implemented to provide employment opportunities for local residents, particularly those who may have been displaced by the redevelopment. Community benefits agreements, which are contracts between developers and community organizations, can also be used to ensure that the benefits of the project are shared with the community.

However, implementing these strategies can also present challenges. For example, affordable housing requirements may be met with resistance from developers who argue that it will increase the cost of the project. Job training programs may also face challenges in finding suitable employment opportunities for participants. It is important to address these challenges and find solutions that balance the needs of all stakeholders involved.

In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment has the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, but it is important to consider the potential social impacts of these projects. By promoting social equity and involving the community in the redevelopment process, we can ensure that these projects not only benefit the environment and economy, but also the well-being of all members of the community.


### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss the various ways in which brownfield redevelopment can affect social equity.

In order to address these potential social impacts, it is important for brownfield redevelopment projects to prioritize social equity. This means involving community members in the decision-making process and considering their needs and concerns. It also means ensuring that the benefits of the project are shared equitably among all members of the community, rather than just benefiting a select few.

### Subsection: 12.1b Role of Social Equity in Brownfield Redevelopment

Social equity should be a key consideration in all stages of brownfield redevelopment, from site selection to project design and implementation. By involving community members in the decision-making process, developers can gain a better understanding of the needs and concerns of the community and work towards addressing them. This can help prevent displacement and ensure that the project benefits the entire community, rather than just a select few.

In addition, developers should also consider the potential health impacts of the project on nearby residents. This means conducting thorough environmental assessments and implementing measures to mitigate any potential negative effects on the community's health. This could include using environmentally-friendly remediation techniques and implementing green infrastructure to reduce pollution and improve air and water quality.

Furthermore, social equity can also be promoted through the creation of affordable housing and job opportunities for low-income and minority community members. This can help prevent displacement and ensure that the benefits of the project are accessible to all members of the community. In addition, developers can also work with local organizations and businesses to provide training and employment opportunities for community members, promoting economic growth and social mobility.

In conclusion, social equity plays a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment. By prioritizing social equity, developers can ensure that these projects not only bring economic and environmental benefits, but also promote social well-being and equity within the community. 


### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss the various ways in which brownfield redevelopment can affect social equity.

#### 12.1a Overview of Social Impacts

Before delving into the specific social impacts of brownfield redevelopment, it is important to define the concept of social equity. Social equity refers to the fair distribution of resources, opportunities, and privileges among all members of a society. This includes access to education, healthcare, housing, and employment, among other things. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, social equity means ensuring that all members of a community, regardless of their socioeconomic status or race, have equal access to the benefits and opportunities that come with these projects.

One of the main social impacts of brownfield redevelopment is the potential displacement of low-income and minority communities. This can result in the displacement of these communities, leading to a loss of social ties and community cohesion.

The remediation process can release harmful pollutants into the air and water, potentially causing health issues for nearby residents. In addition, the construction and operation of new developments can also contribute to noise and air pollution, further impacting the quality of life for residents.

In order to address these potential social impacts, it is important for brownfield redevelopment projects to prioritize social equity. This can be achieved through community engagement and involvement in the planning and decision-making process. By involving all members of the community, especially those who may be most affected by the project, their voices and concerns can be heard and addressed.

#### 12.1b Case Studies in Social Equity and Brownfield Redevelopment

To further illustrate the importance of social equity in brownfield redevelopment, let's take a look at some case studies.

One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Baltimore, Maryland. This site was once a major source of employment for the surrounding community, but after its closure in 2012, it became a brownfield site. The redevelopment project, led by the community and local government, focused on creating job opportunities for the local residents, many of whom were low-income and minority individuals. This not only provided economic benefits, but also helped to preserve the social fabric of the community.

Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Cabrini-Green public housing project in Chicago, Illinois. This project was known for its high levels of poverty and crime, and its demolition in the early 2000s displaced many low-income and minority families. However, the redevelopment project aimed to create a mixed-income community, with affordable housing options for low-income residents. This not only provided housing opportunities for those who were displaced, but also helped to create a more diverse and inclusive community.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. By prioritizing the needs and concerns of the community, these projects can not only bring economic and environmental benefits, but also promote social equity and inclusivity. 


### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss strategies for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment.

#### 12.2a Overview of Social Equity Strategies

Before delving into specific strategies, it is important to understand the underlying principles of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. These principles include community involvement, transparency, and accountability. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. Additionally, holding developers accountable for meeting social equity goals can help ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are distributed fairly among all members of the community.

One strategy for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment is through the use of community benefits agreements (CBAs). CBAs are legally binding agreements between developers and community organizations that outline specific benefits and commitments that the developer will provide to the community in exchange for their support of the project. These benefits can include affordable housing, job training programs, and environmental remediation efforts. By involving community organizations in the negotiation process, CBAs can help ensure that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed and that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably.

Another strategy is to prioritize the hiring of local residents and minority-owned businesses for the construction and operation of the redevelopment project. This can help create job opportunities for members of the community who may have been negatively impacted by the brownfield site in the past. Additionally, developers can work with local organizations to provide job training programs and apprenticeships to help prepare community members for these job opportunities.

In order to address potential displacement of low-income and minority communities, developers can also incorporate affordable housing into the redevelopment project. This can help ensure that residents are not forced to leave their homes due to rising property values. In addition, developers can work with community organizations to provide relocation assistance and support for those who may be displaced.

To mitigate potential health impacts on nearby residents, developers can implement measures to reduce pollution during the remediation and construction process. This can include using environmentally-friendly remediation techniques and implementing green building practices for new developments. Additionally, developers can work with community organizations to monitor air and water quality during and after the project to ensure that the health of residents is not compromised.

Overall, promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment requires a collaborative effort between developers, community organizations, and local government. By incorporating these strategies and principles, brownfield redevelopment projects can not only bring economic and environmental benefits, but also promote social equity and improve the overall well-being of the community.


### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss strategies for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment.

#### 12.2a Overview of Social Equity Strategies

Before delving into specific strategies, it is important to understand the underlying principles of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. These principles include community involvement, transparency, and accountability. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. Additionally, holding developers accountable for meeting social equity goals can help ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are distributed fairly among all members of the community.

One strategy for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment is through the use of community benefits agreements (CBAs). CBAs are legally binding agreements between developers and community organizations that outline specific benefits and commitments that the developer will provide to the community in exchange for their support of the project. These benefits can include affordable housing, job training programs, and environmental remediation efforts. By involving community organizations in the negotiation process, CBAs can help ensure that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed and that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably.

Another strategy is to prioritize the hiring of local residents and minority-owned businesses for the construction and operation of the redevelopment project. This can help create job opportunities for those who may have been disproportionately impacted by the presence of the brownfield site. Additionally, providing job training programs and apprenticeships can help build skills and create a more diverse and inclusive workforce.

#### 12.2b Selection of Social Equity Strategies

When selecting social equity strategies for a brownfield redevelopment project, it is important to consider the specific needs and concerns of the community. This can be done through community engagement and needs assessments. By involving community members in the decision-making process, developers can gain a better understanding of the social issues that are most important to the community and tailor their strategies accordingly.

Another factor to consider is the feasibility and effectiveness of different strategies. Some strategies, such as CBAs, may require significant resources and negotiation, while others, such as prioritizing local hiring, may be more easily implemented. It is important to weigh the potential impact and cost of each strategy in order to select the most appropriate ones for the specific project.

In addition, it is important to continuously monitor and evaluate the effectiveness of social equity strategies throughout the project. This can help identify any issues or areas for improvement and allow for adjustments to be made in a timely manner. By regularly communicating with the community and being transparent about the progress of social equity goals, developers can build trust and ensure that the benefits of the project are being distributed fairly.

In conclusion, promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment requires a combination of principles, strategies, and continuous evaluation. By involving the community, being transparent and accountable, and selecting appropriate strategies, developers can help ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are shared equitably among all members of the community. 


### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:

Brownfield redevelopment projects have the potential to bring numerous benefits to a community, including economic growth, job creation, and improved environmental conditions. However, it is important to also consider the potential social impacts of these projects. In this section, we will discuss strategies for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment.

#### 12.2a Overview of Social Equity Strategies

Before delving into specific strategies, it is important to understand the underlying principles of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. These principles include community involvement, transparency, and accountability. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. Additionally, holding developers accountable for meeting social equity goals can help ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are distributed fairly among all members of the community.

One strategy for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment is through the use of community benefits agreements (CBAs). CBAs are legally binding agreements between developers and community organizations that outline specific benefits and commitments that the developer will provide to the community in exchange for their support of the project. These benefits can include affordable housing, job training programs, and environmental remediation efforts. By involving community organizations in the negotiation process, CBAs can help ensure that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed and that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably.

Another strategy is to prioritize the hiring of local residents and minority-owned businesses for the construction and operation of the redevelopment project. This can help create job opportunities for members of the community who may have been disproportionately impacted by the presence of the brownfield. Additionally, it can help stimulate the local economy and promote economic growth within the community.

#### 12.2b Case Studies in Social Equity Strategies

To further illustrate the effectiveness of social equity strategies in brownfield redevelopment, let's examine a few case studies.

One successful example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Lackawanna, New York. The project, led by the Erie County Industrial Development Agency, involved the cleanup and redevelopment of a 1,200-acre brownfield site. As part of the project, the developers entered into a community benefits agreement with local organizations, which included commitments to provide job training programs and prioritize the hiring of local residents for construction and operation jobs. This not only helped address the social impacts of the brownfield, but also provided economic opportunities for the community.

Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Pullman railcar manufacturing site in Chicago, Illinois. The project, led by the Pullman Park Community Development Corporation, involved the cleanup and redevelopment of a 180-acre brownfield site. The developers worked closely with community organizations to create a community benefits agreement that included commitments to provide affordable housing, job training programs, and prioritize the hiring of local residents and minority-owned businesses. This helped address the social impacts of the brownfield and promote economic growth within the community.

These case studies demonstrate the effectiveness of social equity strategies in promoting fair and equitable outcomes in brownfield redevelopment projects. By involving community members in the decision-making process and prioritizing the needs and concerns of the community, developers can ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are distributed fairly and equitably among all stakeholders. 


### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:

Community engagement is a crucial aspect of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. This not only helps to build trust and support for the project, but also ensures that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably among all members of the community.

#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity

Community engagement plays a vital role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. It allows for the voices of community members to be heard and considered in the decision-making process, ensuring that their needs and concerns are taken into account. This is especially important for marginalized and disadvantaged communities, who may be disproportionately affected by brownfield redevelopment projects.

One way to engage the community is through the use of community meetings and forums. These provide a platform for community members to voice their opinions and concerns, and for developers to address them. It is important for these meetings to be accessible and inclusive, with translations and accommodations for those with disabilities if needed. This allows for a diverse range of voices to be heard and for all members of the community to have a say in the project.

Another important aspect of community engagement is education and information sharing. Many community members may not have a background in environmental management or redevelopment, and may not fully understand the potential impacts and benefits of a brownfield redevelopment project. By providing educational materials and information sessions, developers can ensure that community members are well-informed and can make informed decisions about the project.

In addition to community meetings and education, it is also important for developers to actively seek out and engage with community organizations and leaders. These organizations often have a better understanding of the needs and concerns of the community and can serve as a liaison between the community and the developers. By involving these organizations in the decision-making process, developers can ensure that the project benefits the community as a whole and not just a select few.

Overall, community engagement is crucial for promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. It allows for the needs and concerns of the community to be addressed and ensures that the benefits of the project are distributed fairly among all members of the community. By actively involving the community in the decision-making process and being transparent and accountable, developers can build trust and support for the project and create a more equitable outcome for all stakeholders.


### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:

Community engagement is a crucial aspect of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. This not only helps to build trust and support for the project, but also ensures that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably among all members of the community.

#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity

Community engagement plays a vital role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. It allows for the voices of community members to be heard and considered in the decision-making process, ensuring that their needs and concerns are taken into account. This is especially important for marginalized and disadvantaged communities, who may be disproportionately affected by brownfield redevelopment projects.

One way to engage the community is through the use of community meetings and forums. These provide a platform for community members to voice their opinions and concerns, and for developers to address them. It is important for these meetings to be accessible and inclusive, with translations and accommodations for those with disabilities if needed. This allows for a diverse range of voices to be heard and for all members of the community to have a say in the project.

Another important aspect of community engagement is education and information sharing. Many community members may not have a background in environmental management or redevelopment, and may not fully understand the potential impacts and benefits of a brownfield redevelopment project. By providing educational materials and information sessions, developers can ensure that community members are well-informed and can make informed decisions about the project.

In addition to community meetings and education, there are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in social equity. These techniques include:

#### 12.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Social Equity

1. Surveys and questionnaires: These can be used to gather feedback and opinions from community members on the project. Surveys can be distributed online or in person, and can be designed to gather specific information on social equity concerns.

2. Focus groups: These involve bringing together a small group of community members to discuss the project and provide feedback. This allows for more in-depth discussions and can provide valuable insights into the community's concerns and needs.

3. Community workshops: These workshops can be used to educate community members on the project and gather their input on social equity issues. They can also be used to brainstorm solutions and strategies for promoting social equity in the project.

4. Social media and online platforms: These can be used to engage with a larger audience and gather feedback from a diverse range of community members. Social media can also be used to share information and updates on the project, promoting transparency and community involvement.

5. Community advisory boards: These boards consist of community members who are selected to provide input and feedback on the project. They can serve as a liaison between the community and the developers, ensuring that community concerns are addressed and considered in decision-making.

By utilizing these techniques, developers can effectively engage the community in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. It is important for these techniques to be tailored to the specific needs and concerns of the community, and for developers to actively listen and respond to community feedback. This will not only promote social equity, but also foster a sense of ownership and collaboration within the community.


### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:

Community engagement is a crucial aspect of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the decision-making process and being transparent about the goals and potential impacts of the project, developers can ensure that the needs and concerns of all stakeholders are taken into account. This not only helps to build trust and support for the project, but also ensures that the benefits of the project are distributed equitably among all members of the community.

#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity

Community engagement plays a vital role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment. It allows for the voices of community members to be heard and considered in the decision-making process, ensuring that their needs and concerns are taken into account. This is especially important for marginalized and disadvantaged communities, who may be disproportionately affected by brownfield redevelopment projects.

One way to engage the community is through the use of community meetings and forums. These provide a platform for community members to voice their opinions and concerns, and for developers to address them. It is important for these meetings to be accessible and inclusive, with translations and accommodations for those with disabilities if needed. This allows for a diverse range of voices to be heard and for all members of the community to have a say in the project.

Another important aspect of community engagement is education and information sharing. Many community members may not have a background in environmental management or redevelopment, and may not fully understand the potential impacts and benefits of a brownfield redevelopment project. By providing educational materials and information sessions, developers can ensure that community members are well-informed and can make informed decisions about the project.

In addition to community meetings and education, case studies have shown that involving community members in the actual redevelopment process can also promote social equity. This can include hiring local residents for construction jobs, providing training and job opportunities for community members, and incorporating community input into the design and planning of the project. These actions not only promote social equity by providing economic opportunities for community members, but also foster a sense of ownership and pride in the project.

#### 12.3b Case Studies in Community Engagement and Social Equity

There have been numerous successful case studies of community engagement and social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Baltimore, Maryland. The project involved extensive community engagement, including community meetings, surveys, and focus groups, to gather input and address concerns from local residents. The project also prioritized hiring local residents for construction jobs and providing job training programs for community members. As a result, the project not only successfully remediated the contaminated site, but also provided economic opportunities for the surrounding community.

Another example is the redevelopment of the former South Works steel plant site in Chicago, Illinois. This project involved a partnership between the developer and the local community organization to ensure that community members were involved in the planning and decision-making process. The project also included a community benefits agreement, which outlined specific benefits for the community, such as affordable housing and job opportunities. This project not only successfully remediated the brownfield site, but also provided tangible benefits for the surrounding community.

#### 12.3c Lessons Learned and Best Practices for Community Engagement and Social Equity

From these case studies and others, there are several key lessons and best practices that can be applied to future brownfield redevelopment projects. These include:

- Start community engagement early in the planning process and continue throughout the project.
- Use a variety of methods to engage the community, such as meetings, surveys, and focus groups.
- Ensure that community meetings and materials are accessible and inclusive.
- Provide educational materials and information sessions to inform community members about the project.
- Involve community members in the actual redevelopment process, such as through job opportunities and input in the design and planning.
- Consider a community benefits agreement to ensure tangible benefits for the surrounding community.

By following these best practices, developers can promote social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects and ensure that all stakeholders are involved and benefit from the project. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and social equity. We have seen how the redevelopment of contaminated sites can have a significant impact on the surrounding communities, both positive and negative. We have also discussed the importance of considering social equity in the planning and implementation of brownfield redevelopment projects.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for community involvement and engagement in the decision-making process. By involving the community, we can ensure that their voices are heard and their needs are taken into consideration. This can help to address any potential social equity issues that may arise from the redevelopment project.

Another important aspect to consider is the potential displacement of low-income and marginalized communities. As we have seen, brownfield redevelopment can lead to gentrification and the displacement of these communities. It is crucial to have policies and strategies in place to mitigate these effects and ensure that these communities are not further marginalized.

Furthermore, we have discussed the importance of incorporating social equity into the overall sustainability goals of a brownfield redevelopment project. By promoting social equity, we can create more sustainable and resilient communities that benefit all members of society.

In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment and social equity are closely intertwined, and it is essential to consider both aspects in the planning and implementation of these projects. By doing so, we can create more equitable and sustainable communities for all.
